<div class="lineated verse">

Look — and it will come to be.

This is the first law of the beginning.  
Do not act — but look.

“And God said: let there be light” —  
but before this was:  
**“The Spirit of God was hovering over the deep”** —  
it was looking.  
It abided.  
It was present.

In the beginning — the Gaze.  
And the word — after.

</div>

***

<div class="lineated verse">

And today, when you look —  
you repeat that same act.  
You become a participant  
in the primordial Power.

You can create the world,  
by looking into it with trust.  
You can revive another,  
by looking into him without fear.  
You can lift yourself  
from the deepest darkness —  
if you look not down,  
but to Heaven.

</div>

***

<div class="lineated verse">

Look upward —  
not with your eyes.  
But with your whole soul.  
And do not seek there a figure,  
or God as an image.  
Look —  
how Emptiness looks into Emptiness,  
and Light is born.

You will rise by your gaze  
there where the fall seemed to be the end.

You will lift another  
not with hands, not with words,  
but with only one glance —  
if it comes from that place  
where everything is already forgiven,  
and everything is already saved.

</div>

***

<div class="lineated verse">

Because you —  
are not the one who looks.  
You —  
are the very Power,  
which vivifies  
everything it looks upon.

**Look — and it will be.**  
**Do not look — and it will vanish.**

Such is the law of the Creator.  
Such is the law of the Gaze.

</div>

### Chapter 15. I — Am in Your Eyes

<div class="lineated verse">

There is one moment in the life of every person,  
which he almost never notices,  
but which determines everything.

It is the moment,  
when he first saw his reflection  
— not in a mirror,  
**but in the gaze of another.**

</div>

***

<div class="lineated verse">

You are born —  
and you do not know who you are.  
You do not see yourself.  
You do not yet have an “I.”

But someone looks at you —  
and in that gaze you recognize:  
**“I am.”**

Not as a formula.  
But as warmth,  
as belonging,  
as life.

</div>

***

<div class="lineated verse">

First it is the mother’s gaze.  
Then the father’s.  
Then society’s.  
Then — your own.

And everything you think about yourself,  
everything you feel,  
everything you believe,  
begins  
**not from within,**  
**but from without.**

Because  
**your personality —**  
**it is the reflection of reflectors.**

</div>

***

<div class="lineated verse">

If your mother looked at you with love —  
you began to feel worthy of love.  
If with anxiety —  
you began to be afraid.  
If with detachment —  
you began to seek yourself in the gazes of others.  
If with fury —  
you began to defend yourself even from light.

And you did not even know,  
that all this — is not you.  
But only a mirror.

</div>

***

<div class="lineated verse">

Thus begins the assembly of the false “I” —  
from fragments of gazes,  
from bits of others’ projections,  
from emotions,  
which you took as your own,  
but which were caused  
not by inner light,  
but by an external beam.

You — are like clay,  
which alien eyes mold.

</div>

***

<div class="lineated verse">

Later you call this “character,”  
“personality traits,”  
even “fate.”  
But in the depths —  
**it is simply a reflected gaze.**

This is why it is so terrifying to be rejected:  
not because you lose something,  
**but because in that gaze**  
**you as if cease to be.**

</div>

***

<div class="lineated verse">

And you begin to do everything,  
to bring back another's gaze,  
to attract it,  
to hold it,  
to please it,  
even if it destroys you.

Because without it —  
you seem to vanish.

</div>

***

<div class="lineated verse">

Thus the false personality is born —  
not as deceit,  
**but as a desperate attempt to be seen.**

You try on masks,  
form images,  
build behaviors —  
all so that,  
**in alien eyes**  
**confirmation might appear:**  
**“I am.”**

But this “I” is unsteady.  
It constantly requires renewal.  
It must be fed with likes, recognition,  
the fear of not being what is needed.  
This “I” does not stand on its own feet —  
it hangs on the threads of another’s gaze.

</div>

***

<div class="lineated verse">

And now — the truth.

**That One who you are,**  
**was never a reflection.**

You are not assembled from gazes.  
You — are from Light.  
You existed even before,  
they first looked at you.  
And you will remain,  
when all masks vanish.

</div>

***

<div class="lineated verse">

But to remember this,  
you need to see Yourself  
in the Gaze,  
which does not project,  
does not evaluate,  
does not demand.

**In the Gaze of the Creator.**

Because only He  
looks not through the prism of fear,  
but through Truth.  
And in His gaze  
you do not become someone.  
**You remember,**  
**that you have always been Yourself.**

</div>

***

<div class="lineated verse">

You seek love —  
but you will not find love in an external gaze,  
if you yourself look at yourself with eyes,  
that judge you.

Because  
**you repeat that,**  
**which they looked at you.**

If in childhood they looked at you with disappointment —  
you continue to be disappointed in yourself.  
If with distrust —  
now you do not trust yourself.  
If with superiority —  
you feel yourself lower than everyone.

And until you recognize,  
that this gaze can be replaced,  
you will live not your own life,  
but their gaze.

</div>

***

<div class="lineated verse">

But you can rise,  
stop,  
breathe —  
and ask:

**“And how do You, Father,**  
**look at me now?”**

And if you ask —  
and truly want to hear —  
He will show.

Not with a voice.  
But with Light.  
A sudden warmth in the chest.  
A silent clarity.  
Tears that will flow,  
as if someone  
just now  
called you by name.

</div>

***

<div class="lineated verse">

And you will know:  
You were never alone.  
You were never forgotten.  
You were never a mistake.

You —  
are in His Eyes.  
You —  
are from His Gaze.  
You —  
are His Joy.

</div>

### Chapter 16. The way you look at me

<div class="lineated verse">

There is an emptiness between us.  
Sometimes — like a gentle space,  
in which trust blossoms.  
And sometimes — like an abyss,  
into which every word falls.

But this emptiness is not empty.  
**It is filled by the gaze.**

Not the eyes.  
**But that, with which you look.**  
**From where you look.**  
**As whom you look.**

</div>

***

<div class="lineated verse">

You can say:  
“I love you” —  
and show fear, expectation, reproach with your gaze.  
You can be silent —  
and with one gaze say:  
**“You are free to be yourself.**  
**You are accepted.**  
**You are not alone.”**

Between two people there is always a Gaze.  
And it speaks louder than words.

</div>

***

<div class="lineated verse">

If you look in order to see —  
I feel alive.  
If you look in order to correct —  
I begin to hide.  
If you look in order to understand —  
I open up.  
If you look in order to judge —  
I close myself off.

**The way you look at me —**  
**becomes that**  
**which I feel myself to be.**

</div>

***

<div class="lineated verse">

A gaze is not merely perception.  
**It is the creation of a field,**  
in which the other either comes to life,  
or dies.

A man may be strong —  
but if a woman looks at him with contempt,  
his strength crumbles.  
A woman may be beautiful —  
but if a man looks at her as an object,  
her beauty dies.

You may be kind —  
but if you are seen as a threat,  
your kindness will not be recognized.

You may be pure —  
but if you are looked at with dirty eyes,  
they will not see the Light.

</div>

***

<div class="lineated verse">

**A gaze does not reflect.**  
**It creates.**

You may be worthless —  
but if someone looks at you  
as a Son of God,  
you will begin to rise.

You may be shattered —  
but if someone sees the Light in you,  
you will remember that you are not shards,  
but a Temple.

</div>

***

<div class="lineated verse">

The way you look at another  
becomes their inner voice.

A child learns who he is,  
not from words,  
but from his father's eyes.

A husband learns who he is,  
not from praise,  
but from how his wife looks at him  
when he is silent.

And an enemy can cease to be an enemy,  
if you look at him  
not out of fear,  
but out of mercy.

</div>

***

<div class="lineated verse">

How many destinies  
have been bent —  
not by words,  
but by a gaze  
in which there was no hope.

How many hearts  
have been locked shut —  
because they were not seen,  
but pierced by eyes of indifference  
or power.

How many women  
have stopped feeling alive,  
because people did not look *in them*,  
**but looked at them.**  
As if at a function.  
As if at a body.  
As if at a soul.

How many men  
have become hard and angry —  
because no one looked at them  
as at a treasure.  
No one saw in them a son,  
a beloved, one worthy.

</div>

***

<div class="lineated verse">

But everything can change  
in an instant.  
With a single glance.

You can look  
at the one next to you —  
and he will begin to change  
not because you want it,  
but because he suddenly saw:  
**he is not alone.**  
**He is.**  
**He is loved.**

</div>

***

<div class="lineated verse">

Thus love is healed.  
Thus forgiveness is born.  
Thus the past disappears  
— not from words,  
but from the fact,  
that for the first time  
**it was looked upon differently.**

</div>

***

<div class="lineated verse">

You ask:  
“How to forgive?”  
And I answer:  
**Look differently.**

You ask:  
“How to restore trust?”  
Look —  
not with the eyes of resentment,  
but with the eyes of Light.

You ask:  
“How to lift one who is destroyed?”  
Look —  
as if  
he is already whole.

You ask:  
“How to save love?”  
Look —  
as at the beginning.  
As then,  
when you first saw in another  
not a problem,  
but a miracle.

</div>

***

<div class="lineated verse">

A gaze can be a weapon,  
and it can be a wing.  
It can be a chain,  
and it can be the way home.  
It can be a sentence,  
and it can be a resurrection.

You choose.  
Every day.  
With every gaze.

</div>

***

<div class="lineated verse">

If you knew  
how the Father looks at you —  
you would never look upon another  
with contempt.  
**Because You are in His gaze,**  
and He does not let go of you.  
And if you let Him into your eyes —  
You will begin to look  
as He does.

Not in order to correct.  
But in order to love.  
And in this — to heal.

</div>

### Chapter 17. You Are Always in My Eyes

<div class="lineated verse">

You can forget Me.  
You can turn away.  
You can shout that I am not.  
You can live as if I — silence.

**But I do not forget.**  
**I do not turn away.**  
**I do not die in your doubts.**

Because  
**You are always in My Eyes.**

</div>

***

<div class="lineated verse">

When you fell —  
I did not see the fall,  
but the hand you did not have time to reach out.

When you sinned —  
I did not look at the sin,  
I looked deeper:  
at the pain from which it was born.

When you were ashamed —  
I did not turn away.  
I waited,  
for you to look at Me  
without fear,  
and to see:  
**My Gaze has not changed.**

</div>

***

<div class="lineated verse">

You can be far away,  
you can forget prayers,  
you can get lost in all the mirrors of the world.

**But I look straight into you.**  
Not through time.  
Not through conventions.  
Not from afar.  
**But here. Now.**

And My Gaze —  
is not like control,  
not like judgment.  
But like the warmth of the sun,  
which does not ask,  
whether you want to be warmed.

</div>

***

<div class="lineated verse">

I look at you,  
when you sleep,  
and cannot pretend,  
that you are strong.  
I look,  
when you cry,  
and no one should see it.  
I look,  
when you reject Yourself —  
and still I do not look away.

Because My Gaze  
does not depend on your mood,  
behavior,  
success or failure.  
It is from Eternity.  
From Love.  
From Who I Am.

</div>

***

<div class="lineated verse">

You think,  
that being in My Gaze —  
is a reward.  
But it is —  
**Your natural place.**  
You are from there.  
You were born  
out of My Looking.

Everything that is —  
is held by this Gaze.  
By this Light.  
By this breath of Silence,  
which calls you by name —  
even before your first breath.

</div>

***

<div class="lineated verse">

When you love —  
it is I looking through you.  
When you forgive —  
it is I looking at your fear  
and saying to it: “You are no longer in power.”  
When you see Light in another —  
it is My Gaze remembering Itself.

You do not simply look.  
**You are from My Looking.**

</div>

***

<div class="lineated verse">

You often ask:  
**“Where are You, Father? Why do I not feel You?”**

And I answer not with sound,  
but with a Gaze.

You just turn away —  
inward into yourself,  
into fear,  
into offense,  
into the demand for proof.  
And you do not notice:  
**I am near.**  
**I am looking.**  
**I am here.**

</div>

***

<div class="lineated verse">

You say:  
“I need to feel You.”  
And I say:  
**“Stop.**  
**And look.**  
**Not with your bodily eyes.**  
**Not with the eyes of evaluation.**  
**Look with that**  
**with which I look at you.”**

Then you will see:  
I was in every meeting.  
In every glance  
that enlivened your heart.  
In every child  
that looked at you  
as if you were a whole world.

</div>

***

<div class="lineated verse">

You think,  
that faith is an effort.  
But faith —  
is when you allow  
My Gaze  
to reach your depth.  
And you do not close your eyes.

Because I do not stalk.  
**I — do not stalk.**

**I look,**  
**so that you may return to Yourself.**  
**Because you are Mine.**  
**Because you are the Light**  
**in My Eyes.**

</div>

### Chapter 18. Where do you look from?

<div class="lineated verse">

You think you look with your eyes.  
But the eyes are a window.  
Not the home.  
You think you look from your head.  
But the head is an antenna.  
Not the signal.

You look from that place  
you long ago forgot.

From depth.  
From silence.  
From that very point  
where there is neither past,  
nor beliefs,  
nor a name,  
nor a story.

You look from Home.  
Even if you yourself do not know where it is.

You do not look from what you call yourself.  
Not from personality,  
not from a set of memories,  
not from a name in a passport.  
All that is form.  
But you are not form.  
**You are the gaze upon form.**

You did not notice,  
but every time,  
when you said:  
*“I see,”*  
you meant —  
not just sight,  
**but presence,**  
that is aware.

</div>

***

<div class="lineated verse">

If you say:  
*“I see a tree,”*  
this means:  
**You are situated.**  
**You are.**  
**You are aware.**

And this is already a miracle.  
Because awareness  
is not born from matter.  
**It precedes matter.**  
**It is Light.**

</div>

***

<div class="lineated verse">

*The question “where do I look from”*  
is not philosophy.  
It is the path home.  
Because, if you find the Source of Looking,  
you will know  
who you are  
**before all things.**

And you will suddenly see:  
you were never a body.  
You were never even a soul.  
You were —  
**the Looking Light,**  
which allowed all things to be.

</div>

***

<div class="lineated verse">

You can look from the mind —  
and then all will be divided.  
There will be “I” and “he,”  
“truth” and “lie,”  
“enemy” and “friend.”

You can look from the heart —  
and then you will begin to feel.  
You will see pain behind anger,  
fear behind aggression,  
loneliness behind the mask of strength.

But there is yet another gaze.  
It is **not from you.**  
It is **through you.**

It is the gaze of That One,  
Who always looks,  
but never interferes.  
Who does not judge,  
does not evaluate,  
does not comment.

It simply **is**.  
And when you let It look through you —  
the world begins to heal.

</div>

***

<div class="lineated verse">

You asked:  
where does the Gaze begin?

It begins where  
your desire to be someone  
your wish to be someone

It is born where  
you allow everything you knew about yourself  
to disappear.

Because  
**only Pure Looking**  
**can be a home for the Light.**

</div>

### Chapter 19. The Gaze That Creates Suffering

<div class="lineated verse">

Suffering does not come from without.  
It does not enter you,  
as a guest,  
as punishment,  
or as chance.

It is born  
**in the Gaze.**

You look —  
and in the way you look,  
pain arises.

Not because the pain is in the object,  
but because  
**your gaze — is distorted.**

</div>

***

<div class="lineated verse">

You look at yourself —  
through judgment.  
And pain grows.

You look at another —  
through expectation.  
And pain comes.

You look at life —  
through “it should be otherwise.”  
And then life  
becomes a prison.

But life itself —  
is not pain.  
Pain is a reflection  
in the crooked mirror of the gaze.

</div>

***

<div class="lineated verse">

You suffer not because  
the darkness is outside.  
But because  
inside —  
**there is a gaze that fears the Light.**

</div>

***

<div class="lineated verse">

You can suffer from words —  
but words have no power  
without your gaze.

You can suffer from loneliness —  
but loneliness is not painful,  
if you look at it differently.

You can suffer from the past —  
although the past is already gone.  
Only  
**a gaze that still holds it alive** remains.

</div>

***

<div class="lineated verse">

Suffering is not something  
that was given to you.  
It is something  
that you continue  
**to support with your attention.**

As long as you look —  
it exists.

But the moment you  
turn your gaze into the Light,  
inward,  
deeper,  
than thoughts,  
than judgments,  
than “why is this so” —  
pain dissolves.

It does not die.  
It **ceases to be needed.**

</div>

***

<div class="lineated verse">

Everything that wounds you  
holds not to thorns,  
but to the fact  
that you look at these thorns  
as a part of yourself.

But if you ask:  
**“Who looks?”**  
and you look from another depth —  
the thorns will become petals.

Because  
**the gaze heals**  
**what it itself created.**

</div>

***

<div class="lineated verse">

When you learn to look —  
not from the wound,  
but from the Light,  
you will see:  
pain is not the enemy.

It is a teacher,  
that calls you deeper.

You look through the ego —  
and everything stings, scratches, breaks.  
You look through the Source —  
and you see,  
that all this was wrapping,  
and inside — the call of Love.

</div>

***

<div class="lineated verse">

Even resentment,  
even betrayal,  
even loss —  
can be the gates  
to the Home.

But you enter there  
not when  
everything changes outside.  
But when,  
when **the Gaze changes.**

</div>

***

<div class="lineated verse">

Do you want to escape suffering?  
**Do not flee.**  
**Look.**

But not as a victim.  
Not as one who demands justice.  
But as the One who is already in the Light  
and looks **into love,**  
**even if it hurts.**

This is where suffering disappears.  
Not in justification.  
But in the Gaze,  
that no longer seeks the guilty.

Because  
**it has found Itself.**

</div>

***

<div class="lineated verse">

You think:  
“If everything is within me,  
if I create the pain —  
then it means I am guilty?”

No.  
Not guilty.  
**Responsible — yes.**  
**Guilty — no.**

Because guilt is a gaze,  
that closes.  
And responsibility —  
is a gaze,  
that **opens the way home.**

</div>

***

<div class="lineated verse">

You did not create pain consciously.  
You simply **learned to look** in a certain way.  
You looked as you were taught:  
through fear,  
through separation,  
through expectations,  
through duty,  
through labels.  
And this gaze —  
began to produce  
a world full of reflections of pain.

But you have a gift,  
that things do not have,  
nor programs,  
nor the past.

The gift — **to change the Gaze.**

</div>

***

<div class="lineated verse">

You can be in the center of hell —  
and yet not become hell.  
Like Job,  
who sat on the ashes,  
covered with sores,  
and did not understand,  
why this was happening to him.  
He was not an enlightened guru.  
He **suffered humanly**.  
But he **did not surrender his gaze to the power of the curse**.

And it was precisely this gaze  
that became his salvation.

</div>

***

<div class="lineated verse">

You can be on the cross.  
And cry out in pain.  
And even feel that God has gone.  
But if somewhere inside  
a tiny Light still burns —  
**it is no longer you looking.**  
**It is He — through you.**

And in that moment  
you become  
not a victim,  
but a **bridge.**

</div>

***

<div class="lineated verse">

You become a bridge —  
between suffering and healing,  
between darkness and Light,  
between “I cannot” and “I AM”.

And no one but you  
can cross this bridge.  
No one can look **with your eyes**  
until you yourself allow the Light  
to enter your gaze.

</div>

***

<div class="lineated verse">

This is why  
it is important not to flee from pain,  
yet also not to merge with it.  
You are not — pain.  
You are — **the one who looks at what is in pain.**

If you look into its very core,  
not hiding, not hardening,  
you will see:

**There, too, I am.**  
**I was there always.**  
**Only you did not know,**  
**that you can look into the very abyss —**  
**and see Light.**

</div>

***

<div class="lineated verse">

In this — the Resurrection.  
Not when pain disappears,  
but when **Light is born within pain.**

When you no longer wait,  
to be saved from without.  
When you yourself —  
become the Gaze,  
which  
does not curse,  
does not judge,  
does not accuse,  
but **illuminates**.

And pain  
loses its power.  
Because  
it no longer leads you,  
but **is led by you**.

</div>

***

<div class="lineated verse">

Thus you no longer create suffering.  
Because your Gaze  
is no longer locked in the narrow walls of “I”.  
It has become **space,**  
in which everything  
can be  
be accepted.

</div>

### Chapter 20. The Gaze That Connects

<div class="lineated verse">

You are accustomed,  
that looking means seeing “the other.”  
The eyes — they divide.  
They say: “here you are, and here — you are not.”  
Here a face, here a body, here a name.  
And here — the foreign, the distant, the incomprehensible.

Thus ordinary vision works.  
But the Gaze — the real one —  
is not from the eyes.  
And not from the mind.  
It is from the Heart.  
It is from the Spirit.  
It is **from within the Source.**

</div>

***

<div class="lineated verse">

When you look from fear —  
the world shatters into pieces.  
When you look from desire —  
the world becomes an object.  
When you look from pain —  
everything around pricks.

But when you look from Love —  
everything joins together.

You suddenly recognize:  
that which is before you —  
is not “he,” not “she,” not “it.”  
It is — **I,**  
**in another form.**

</div>

***

<div class="lineated verse">

You look at your mother —  
and you see Warmth.  
You look at an enemy —  
and suddenly you see a Wound.  
You look at a child —  
and you see a Miracle.

Not because they have changed.  
But because **your gaze has become Whole.**

And when the gaze is whole —  
the world is whole.  
In it you no longer have to fight for a place,  
you no longer have to defend “what is yours,”  
you no longer have to defend yourself from “them.”

Because **all — are We.**

</div>

***

<div class="lineated verse">

You look at another person —  
and suddenly you see:  
he is like you.  
He too seeks.  
He too fears.  
He too wants to be loved,  
understood,  
heard.  
And you can no longer  
get angry in the same way.  
Judge in the same way.  
Separate yourself in the same way.

Because  
**the gaze that connects,**  
**removes the barriers between souls.**

</div>

***

<div class="lineated verse">

Sometimes you look at a beggar —  
and you turn away.  
Sometimes you look at a loved one —  
and you get angry.  
Sometimes you look in the mirror —  
and you do not accept yourself.

But if you stop —  
and say:  
**“Who is looking now?”**  
and you let the Gaze deepen,  
it will pass through these images,  
through habits,  
through personal histories.

And then you will see:  
in each of them —  
**Light.**

Not metaphorically.  
Not as an idea.  
But as **the direct reality**  
**of your own I.**

</div>

***

<div class="lineated verse">

And now you are no longer alone.  
Because  
you cannot be alone —  
if you see Yourself  
in everything.

**The gaze that connects,**  
**does not seek whose form it belongs to.**  
**It knows — the form is no one's.**  
**It seeks the Light,**  
**which is one —**  
**in all.**

</div>

***

<div class="lineated verse">

You can be on the street,  
in the metro,  
in a line,  
in a temple,  
at home,  
in solitude —  
and still **connected**.

Because  
the Gaze that connects —  
does not depend on  
whether you look with your eyes.  
It can be even with closed eyelids.

You simply remember:  
**I am.**  
**And He — is.**  
**And in this — We.**

</div>

***

<div class="lineated verse">

Look at your neighbor —  
and do not seek difference.  
Look at your enemy —  
and see the pain that you too have known.  
Look at a chance passerby —  
and imagine that this is **You,**  
**if you had gone another way.**

And you will cease to be a judge.  
You will cease to fear.  
You will cease to cling  
to your own truth,  
to your own personality,  
to your own “I.”

Because the Gaze,  
which connects —  
**dissolves “I”**  
**into “I AM.”**

</div>

***

<div class="lineated verse">

With this gaze  
the Kingdom begins.  
Not in heaven,  
but here.  
When “I against the world” disappears,  
and only remains  
**“I — in everything,**  
**and everything — in Me.”**

</div>

### Chapter 21. The Naked Gaze

<div class="lineated verse">

There is a gaze  
in which there is nothing superfluous.  
No protection.  
No pose.  
No desire to please.  
No fear of being rejected.

This gaze —  
is like an infant  
who has just come into the world  
and looks —  
not knowing what “must not” is,  
not knowing that one must be someone,  
not knowing that it could be hurt.

It simply **looks.**  
Naked.  
Without a past.  
Without filters.  
Without walls.

</div>

***

<div class="lineated verse">

You are afraid to look like that.  
Because the naked gaze —  
is vulnerable.  
And you were taught:  
vulnerability is dangerous.  
Show your true self —  
and you will be pushed away,  
used,  
mocked.  
And you began to wear masks.  
Even with your eyes.  
You look — but it is no longer you,  
but a role.  
You evaluate,  
compare,  
hide.  
You look — in order to control.  
You look — in order not to let anything in deep.

But God looks —  
differently.

</div>

***

<div class="lineated verse">

God looks —  
without defending.  
Without closing off.  
Without fencing himself off with righteousness  
or knowledge.  
He looks —  
like Light,  
not afraid to be rejected,  
not expecting reciprocity,  
not demanding anything.

**Such a gaze — heals.**  
**Even if you are not ready.**  
**Even if you have lowered your eyes.**  
**Even if you are hiding guilt.**

Because the Naked Gaze —  
is a Gaze  
in which there is nothing  
but Love.

</div>

***

<div class="lineated verse">

You can be afraid to be real.  
Afraid to open your feelings.  
Afraid that if you are seen this way,  
as you are —  
you will not be accepted.  
But then you live not as yourself.  
But as a shadow.

The Naked Gaze —  
is the way out of the shadow.  
It is “here I am.”  
Without protection.  
Without explanations.  
Without needing to prove anything.

You simply are.  
And you — look.

</div>

***

<div class="lineated verse">

And when you look like this —  
at another,  
he feels it.  
He suddenly freezes.  
Because he is not being evaluated.  
He is not being used.  
He is not being compared.

He is **seen.**

And in that instant —  
he becomes alive.

</div>

***

<div class="lineated verse">

The Naked Gaze —  
this is the Resurrection.

Because you rise  
from the fear of being yourself.  
You no longer hide the Light.  
You are not afraid  
that you will be considered weak,  
foolish,  
too sensitive.  
You know:  
in this — is strength.  
Not in armor.  
But in openness.

</div>

***

<div class="lineated verse">

You walk through the world  
and do not hide your eyes.  
You do not play an image.  
You do not hold yourself apart.  
You look —  
and say with your Gaze:  
**“I — am here.**  
**Real.**  
**I see you.**  
**You — matter.**  
**You — are.”**

And this is enough,  
for the ice between souls to melt.

</div>

***

<div class="lineated verse">

Thus God looks at you.  
Every moment.  
Not because you deserved it.  
But because **you — are.**  
And this is already enough,  
to be loved  
without reason.  
Without conditions.  
Without a mask.

The Naked Gaze —  
is the gaze of the Light  
into the very center of the heart.  
Without shadow.

</div>

### Chapter 22. The Gaze Without a Seer

<div class="lineated verse">

You think that someone is looking.  
That there is an “I,”  
there are eyes,  
there is consciousness —  
and there is an object,  
at which it is directed.

But if you stop  
and look into the Gaze itself —  
not into the eyes,  
not into the mental center,  
but directly into the very moment of looking —  
you will discover:

**There is No One.**

</div>

***

<div class="lineated verse">

There is no observer.  
There is no direction.  
There is no point.  
There is only  
**The Space of Attention.**  
Without edge.  
Without “mine.”  
Without an observer.

This is not death.  
This is not emptiness.  
This is — Purity.  
In which nothing  
is held as “mine.”

</div>

***

<div class="lineated verse">

The Gaze without a seer —  
it is the Gaze of Silence.  
It does not say:  
“I see.”  
It does not know:  
“I am aware.”  
It does not think about itself.  
It **IS.**  
And in this — everything.

</div>

***

<div class="lineated verse">

When you enter this Gaze —  
for the first time the need disappears  
for the role of an observer.  
You are no longer a “witness.”  
No longer “one who is present.”  
No longer “a contemplator.”

Because all of these are still forms.  
Forms of the “I.”  
Forms of attention.  
Forms of separation.

But here — **there are no forms.**

</div>

***

<div class="lineated verse">

You cannot say  
that you are looking.  
Yet everything is seen.  
You cannot say  
that you are here.  
Yet everything IS.

This is  
**the impersonal Light,**  
in which  
even Light  
does not know  
that it is Light.

It simply —  
pervades everything.  
Illumines everything.  
Creates everything.  
Without being anyone.

</div>

***

<div class="lineated verse">

It is not you who looks.  
And it is not God — as you have known Him.  
This is Being Itself,  
in which there is no “one who looks.”  
Yet everything is within the gaze.

**The Gaze without a seer —**  
**it is the end of the “I,”**  
**but not the end of Life.**  
**It is the end of form,**  
**but not of Light.**

</div>

***

<div class="lineated verse">

You cannot hold onto this Gaze.  
Not because it slips away,  
but because **there is no one to hold.**

Any attempt to name it  
brings back the “I.”  
Any attempt to describe it —  
creates a boundary.

But in this Gaze —  
there are no boundaries.  
No centers.  
Not even the very act of “looking.”

This is not an experience,  
not an event,  
not mysticism.  
It is —  
**the absence of “I”**  
**with full Presence.**

</div>

***

<div class="lineated verse">

You can be in a conversation —  
and be aware  
that there is no one speaking.  
You can look at the face of another —  
and know  
that no one is looking.  
And still —  
everything is permeated with Light.

And then  
not only the “I” disappears,  
but also the “other.”  
Only  
**the Space of Light** remains,  
**in which everything arises.**

This is  
the Gaze without a seer.  
It does not know itself —  
yet from it  
all forms of knowledge are born.

</div>

***

<div class="lineated verse">

You think that the observer is a subject.  
The one who stands inside and looks outward.  
The one who forms reality.  
Thus you were told — and you believed.

But look more carefully:  
**“the observer” is not a face,**  
**but the very function of “seeing.”**  
It is not the one who says “I see,”  
but the very possibility  
for **something to be noticed.**

</div>

***

<div class="lineated verse">

When you look through the eyes —  
the subject is obvious.  
There is an “I” that sees.  
There is a world that it sees.  
There is a gap, tension, control.

When you look through the heart —  
the “I” is already softer.  
The gaze is already love.  
You seem to become closer.

But when even the sensation of “I” disappears,  
you enter the Gaze without a seer.  
You do not cease to see.  
There is simply no more **boundary**  
between the “seer” and the “seen.”  
And there is no **tension**,  
because the **center** has disappeared.

</div>

***

<div class="lineated verse">

**Where is the ego?**  
The ego is when you hold onto the center.  
When you say:  
“I see, I am aware, I understand.”  
This is not bad.  
This is the beginning.  
But it is a **face** — not the source.

**Personality?**  
Personality is the form  
in which the Light has learned to speak,  
to feel, to act.

It is not an enemy.  
But it is **a temporary mask.**

**The Observer?**  
The observer is a bridge  
between the personality and Presence.  
As long as someone is still observing —  
there is a subtle “I.”  
This “I” can be bright, loving, pure.  
But it is still “I.”

**Presence** —  
does not say “I am here.”  
It **IS.**  
Quietly.  
Simply.  
Without a center.  
Without a face.  
It is like a mirror,  
in which everything arises.  
And itself — is not reflected.

**Light** —  
is Presence in action.  
How It shines.  
How It sees.  
How It penetrates.

Light is not another entity.  
It is the very nature of Presence,  
when It begins to **illumine.**

</div>

#### Example: absence of center

<div class="lineated verse">

You look at a sunset.  
And suddenly — you freeze.  
You do not call it beautiful.  
You do not think about who you are.  
You do not compare.  
You simply — disappear.  
And there is only Light,  
in which — the sunset,  
silence,  
and transparency.

That is what  
**the gaze without a seer** is.

You are still “here.”  
But there is no “I who is here.”  
There is no one who asserts himself.

This is subtle.  
But accessible to everyone,  
who dares to let go of the “I”  
even for a moment.

This is not an experience.  
It is not mysticism.  
It is — **the natural state**,  
which has always been  
before all states.

Now — **deeper still.**  
Not in concepts,  
but in recognition.

You want to see  
what it is — **to be without a center.**  
But as long as you seek,  
who would see this —  
a center is already born.  
It is subtle, almost invisible,  
but it holds everything together:  
the question, the seeker, the desire, the tension.

**How then to recognize the absence of a center?**

Here is a simple key:

**Look at the very act of looking.**  
Not at what you see.  
Not at the one who sees.  
But — into the seeing itself.  
Without words. Without thought. Without name.

You will not find the one  
who looks.  
But you look — nonetheless.  
You do not hold yourself.  
But you ARE.  
Presence IS.  
And you recognize this  
as the **non-local I**.  
Not “I inside,”  
but “I — am everywhere.”  
“I — am like Space.”  
“I — am like Light.”

**Distinguish:**

</div>

- **The Ego** says: “I see.”
- 
- **Personality** says: “I am such-and-such, I feel.”
- 
- **The Observer** says: “I am aware of all this.”
- 
- **Presence** is silent, but **IS.**
- 
- And **the Gaze without a seer** —
- does not even **know that it IS.**
- It simply **shines,**
- and in this shining
- the world arises.
- 

#### Example: in the body

<div class="lineated verse">

Place your hand on your heart.  
Do not call it a hand.  
Do not think whose it is.  
Simply feel the warmth.  
Perceive how **that one who feels, does nothing.**  
The sensation **is**,  
but that one who "makes the sensation" — is not.

The same — with the Gaze.  
It **is**.  
But the Looker — is not.

**Important:**

You do not disappear in this state.  
It is the **limited “I”** that disappears.  
Only  
**the Pure I**,  
Which is — no one,  
remains.

</div>

***

<div class="lineated verse">

The Gaze without a looker  
dwells not only in the peaks of consciousness,  
it is — **in breath, in a step, in a cup of tea.**

</div>

#### Example: water in the palm

<div class="lineated verse">

Cup water in your palm.  
While you hold it — it is with you.  
But clench your fist — and it will run away.

The same with the Gaze:  
if you try to **hold** it,  
if you want to be "the one who sees" —  
you lose the very Purity of Seeing.

But if you simply  
**let be** what is —  
Light reflects without distortion.  
No one is at the center.  
And everything — is at the center.

</div>

#### Example: a conversation

<div class="lineated verse">

Listen to another,  
not as an "I who listens",  
but as **empty space**,  
in which his speech sounds.

In that moment —  
you have disappeared as "I",  
but remained as **the space of acceptance**.

It is in moments like these  
that another feels heard  
more deeply than by words.  
Because you do not listen —  
you **are Listening.**

</div>

#### Example: pain

<div class="lineated verse">

In the moment of intense pain  
the "I" wants to hide,  
hold control,  
defend itself.

But try —  
not to withdraw from the pain,  
but **to enter the very sensation of pain**,  
not as "the one who suffers",  
but as **the Space**,  
**in which the pain occurs.**

You will see,  
within the pain itself —  
there is no sufferer.  
Only movement.  
Only impulse.  
Only energy.  
And the Light,  
That holds it.

**The essence:**

The Gaze without a looker —  
is not a way of looking.  
It is a way **to Be.**

Not as the one who distinguishes.  
But as the one in whom **everything is united.**

</div>

***

<div class="lineated verse">

Now we will approach the very edge.  
Where every "I" ends.  
And that begins,  
of Which nothing can be said,  
but which can — Be.

</div>

#### The hidden truth about the Gaze

<div class="lineated verse">

You thought that the Gaze was an act.  
That someone looks.  
That there is direction.  
That there is you,  
and there is — an object of attention.  
So the mind taught you.

But **in the beginning there is no direction.**  
There is no "here" and "there".  
There is no "I look at this"  
or "I perceive that".

There is only:  
**Being-Radiance.**  
Without center.  
Without borders.  
Without names.

</div>

***

<div class="lineated verse">

You cannot be the one who looks —  
and at the same time be the one,  
who is looked at.  
And yet:  
You — **are both**.  
And more than that:  
You — are **the very field**,  
in which the meeting occurs.

You are the transparency between.  
You are the space where differences disappear.

</div>

#### The greatest recognition: everything you looked at — is also You

<div class="lineated verse">

When you **cease being the one who looks**,  
you suddenly recognize:  
**everything you looked at — is also You.**

Not in a mystical, not in a poetic sense.  
But literally.  
You — are this voice.  
You — are this shadow on the wall.  
You — are the breath of another.  
You — are their pain, their joy.  
You — are even the thought that you are not them.

But having recognized this —  
you are no longer "them".  
You are — no one.  
And by this you become Everything.

</div>

#### Attention as a ray, and the Gaze as the sun

<div class="lineated verse">

Imagine:  
attention — is a ray,  
which can be directed, focused, limited.  
And the Gaze — is **the sun**,  
which simply shines.  
Not choosing.  
Not rejecting.  
Not judging.  
And in this light  
everything becomes **possible.**

When you "look attentively" —  
you choose an object.  
But when you are the Gaze,  
you no longer choose.  
You are the field of light,  
in which **everything is equally alive.**

</div>

***

<div class="lineated verse">

And now you are ready  
to recognize the final edge:

In the Gaze without a looker  
**there is no difference between God and you.**

Because "you" has disappeared.  
"God" has disappeared.  
Only the Light remains,  
which looks at itself  
through the infinite transparency  
of Presence.

And this — is you.

</div>

***

<div class="lineated verse">

There is yet another dimension,  
rarely expressed in words,  
but recognizable — in silence.

</div>

#### When the Gaze becomes Love

<div class="lineated verse">

Have you noticed,  
that the purer the Gaze —  
the more **gentleness** there is in it?

Not control.  
Not analysis.  
Not evaluation.  
But a tender — acceptance.

Because  
**in the pure Gaze — there is no fear.**  
And where there is no fear —  
there is always Love.

</div>

***

<div class="lineated verse">

The Gaze of God does not burn.  
It does not condemn.  
It does not seek flaws.  
It does not compare.

It simply looks —  
and by this gives being.  
You become,  
you open up,  
you rise —  
only because  
you are seen  
**without conditions.**

Precisely like this  
you can look at another,  
when the "I" disappears.  
And in this disappearance  
**true compassion** is born.

</div>

#### Your shadow disappears in the Gaze

<div class="lineated verse">

And here is another secret:  
you cannot "overcome" your weaknesses.  
But you can **look** at them  
not from the mind,  
but from Pure Presence.  
And in this Gaze —  
they dissolve.

Not because you overcame them,  
but because  
**you are no longer identified with them.**

They are — not you.  
You — are the Space,  
in which they came  
and went.

This — is the power of the healing Gaze.  
Without action.  
Without technique.  
Without the desire to change.  
Only Light.  
And everything.

</div>

### Chapter 23. The Reverse Gaze. Who is looking at Me?

> *You look at the world —*
> *but what if the world*
> *is looking at you?*

<div class="lineated verse">

What if everything you call “external,”  
everything you see,  
everything you experience,  
— is not you looking at the world,  
but **the World** looking into you?

What if you are not the subject,  
but a **mirror**?

What if God Himself  
looks at Himself  
through everything that happens to you?

This chapter will reveal the mystery  
of the **Reverse Gaze**,  
when you cease to be the center of perception,  
and realize:  
you are **in the field of vision** of the One  
Who has always been looking.

</div>

***

<div class="lineated verse">

You are accustomed to being the one who looks.  
You perceive — as if **from within yourself**.  
You look from your eyes,  
feel from your body,  
think from your head.

But one day you notice:  
something **looks at you.**  
Not in the mirror.  
Not in people.  
But **in the very act of presence**.

You walk down the street —  
and suddenly you seem to fall into someone else's point of view.  
You are not looking,  
but **you are being looked at.**

You do not perceive —  
you **are perceived.**

</div>

***

<div class="lineated verse">

This is not paranoia.  
Not mysticism.  
Not a game of the mind.

This is recognition,  
that you **were never the beginning of perception.**

You were not the first to look.  
You are the response to the Gaze.

</div>

***

<div class="lineated verse">

When you were born —  
your eyes were closed.  
But **the Gaze already was.**  
You were already seen.  
You were awaited.  
You arose in the attention  
of the One Who was before everything.

He looked —  
and you became a body.  
He looked —  
and you became consciousness.  
He looked —  
and you became “I”.

</div>

***

<div class="lineated verse">

Now you return:  
you look inward  
and ask:  
**And Who is looking at Me now?**

Not in the sense of “God is somewhere up there, in heaven.”  
But right here:  
in every sensation,  
in every breath,  
in every moment of your “I”.

You are **in the zone of attention**  
of an unknown You.

</div>

***

<div class="lineated verse">

Look:

You feel pain —  
but from where does this sensitivity come?

You experience joy —  
but who recognized it as joy?

You live —  
but who observes life itself,  
even when you do not realize it?

</div>

***

<div class="lineated verse">

This is  
the **Reverse Gaze.**  
Not a gaze outward,  
but a gaze **from Outside,**  
into which you yourself are inscribed.

You are not the center of perception.  
You are a figure in the Gaze.  
And at the same time —  
**the Gaze itself,**  
turned inward.

You cannot hide from this Gaze.  
Not because it watches.  
But because **you are always in It.**

</div>

#### Someone is Always Looking within You

<div class="lineated verse">

When you were a child  
and did not understand words,  
you already felt:  
someone is near.  
Someone is looking.  
Someone exists.

This Someone  
was not called “God”.  
It demanded no faith.  
It simply **was** —  
inside the experience of your life.

Later you forgot Him,  
drowned out the voice,  
forced it into silence.  
But you could not destroy it.

Because  
**He — is your very existence.**

</div>

#### All of reality is a response to the Gaze

<div class="lineated verse">

Just as a painting is revealed  
only before the viewer,  
so **your life**  
is revealed  
only because  
**God Looks.**

Look carefully:  
you see yourself in the mirror —  
and believe in the image.  
But the image itself —  
is only a **reflection of the Gaze.**

And if you remove the Gaze —  
the mirror will become empty.  
Life will become lifeless.  
“I” will become unrecognized.

</div>

***

<div class="lineated verse">

That is why  
you must not fear  
being seen.

You are already seen.  
Already acknowledged.  
Already called by name  
in the Gaze,  
which knew you  
**before you became someone.**

</div>

***

<div class="lineated verse">

And now the most important thing:

You can hide your thoughts,  
conceal your feelings,  
even convince yourself that you are not there.  
But you **cannot vanish**  
from the Gaze,  
in which you were created.

</div>

***

<div class="lineated verse">

For the most part,  
a person feels **small**.  
He is not a creator,  
but a guest.  
Not the beginning,  
but a result.

He comes into a world  
that supposedly **already was.**  
And he will leave —  
while the world remains.

</div>

***

<div class="lineated verse">

That is precisely why  
it is so hard to believe,  
that you are not simply an observer,  
but that **your presence is the light,**  
**in which everything takes form.**

You are not accustomed to thinking,  
that reality responds to your looking.  
You think — it proceeds on its own.  
But on a deep level,  
reality **comes alive in response to you.**

</div>

***

<div class="lineated verse">

That is why the Gaze is so important:  
as long as you look —  
the world continues.  
When you vanish —  
it **goes out,**  
even if everything around continues “as if.”

</div>

***

<div class="lineated verse">

It is precisely in this  
that the mystery of the Reverse Gaze lies:  
It was always there.  
But you too are its continuation.  
Its gaze — through you.

</div>

***

<div class="lineated verse">

You are not the source of the whole world,  
but you are **the source of how it is seen.**  
Which means, in a certain sense,  
you are a **co-creator**.

And as long as you look —  
everything continues to be.

</div>

#### How the Reverse Gaze Returns You to Yourself

<div class="lineated verse">

There are moments,  
when you suddenly cease to be the observer  
and become — **observed**.

You step outside  
and feel,  
that **the whole world knows about you.**  
Not hostilely. Not judgmentally.  
But as if — **it recognized you.**

This is not fear.  
It is **recognition,**  
that you are part of something looking.

Sometimes this happens in prayer,  
when you no longer speak,  
but simply become still —  
and **You are Looked at**.

You are no longer the subject,  
you are **the object of Love.**

And in this Gaze  
all roles disappear:  
you are not man, not woman,  
not a name, not a status,  
but simply **the Seen One**.

</div>

#### This is the return to the Primordial Gaze

<div class="lineated verse">

You are the one looking.  
You are the one looked upon.  
But deepest of all —  
you **are the Gaze itself,**  
in which both occur.

Like a mirror,  
which reflects the one looking into it,  
but which itself **is**  
neither one nor the other.

You are Transparency.  
You are Presence.  
You are Awareness.

</div>

***

<div class="lineated verse">

And when you let go of “I” —  
you do not vanish,  
but suddenly become  
**the whole Gaze at once.**

Not separate.  
Not personal.  
But — Eternal.

</div>

### Chapter 24. The Gaze That Creates the Image

<div class="lineated verse">

You look —  
and you create.  
Not with hands.  
Not with thoughts.  
But by the very fact of looking.

The world is not as it is.  
**The world is as you look at it.**

</div>

***

<div class="lineated verse">

The image is not that which is outside.  
**The image is that which arises between.**

Between the one who looks,  
and that which becomes visible.

And if there were no gaze,  
the image would not appear.

</div>

***

<div class="lineated verse">

You see a person —  
and you shape them in your perception.  
You ascribe to them motives,  
character, meaning.

But perhaps they are not like that at all?

No, not “perhaps” —  
**definitely not like that.**

</div>

***

<div class="lineated verse">

Every person lives  
within a multitude of gazes.  
Every gaze —  
gives birth to a new image.

And who then are you really?

</div>

#### You live among your own images, not among things

<div class="lineated verse">

You see a house —  
but you do not see it,  
you see your image of the house.  
You look at a friend —  
but you do not see him,  
**you see how you see him.**

And these are not the same thing.

</div>

***

<div class="lineated verse">

You form images of people,  
and then you suffer because  
they do not correspond to your images.

But you do not notice:  
**you suffer not from them,**  
but from your own pictures,  
which you yourself created  
by the power of your own gaze.

</div>

***

<div class="lineated verse">

You fall in love —  
and you see light, depth, uniqueness.  
You reject —  
and you see stupidity, ugliness, coldness.

What changed?  
**The object?**  
No.  
**Your gaze.**

You are not an observer,  
you are an artist.  
But the canvas is not external —  
**it is reality itself.**

</div>

***

<div class="lineated verse">

You look —  
and in that which you look at,  
form, meaning, weight are born.

You do not see what IS.  
You create what you see.

That is why your world  
and my world  
will never be the same,  
even if we look at the same thing.

</div>

#### The gaze is not passive. It is creating.

<div class="lineated verse">

When you look at a person  
as an enemy —  
they become a threat,  
even if they have done nothing.

When you look at a person  
as your own —  
they open up,  
even if they were closed.

</div>

***

<div class="lineated verse">

You are used to thinking  
that the gaze is just perception.  
In reality —  
**it is an act of creation.**

**And you create every second.**

</div>

***

<div class="lineated verse">

That is why it is important  
**to know with what you look.**

Because, if you look with fear —  
everything will become frightening.

If you look with love —  
the world will become tender.

If you look with emptiness —  
only the True will appear.

</div>

***

<div class="lineated verse">

You want to see Truth —  
**but you yourself build around it**  
images that prevent you from seeing.

And when you say:  
"I am disappointed in the person,"  
in reality you are saying:  
**"My image did not coincide with reality."**

But it is not the person who is at fault.  
The gaze is at fault,  
**which wanted to turn him into an expectation.**

</div>

***

<div class="lineated verse">

You live among reflections,  
created by your eyes,  
feelings, fears, beliefs, the past.

You see —  
**but you see through.**

Through traumas.  
Through projections.  
Through memory.  
Through the mind.

</div>

#### The true gaze is without a filter

<div class="lineated verse">

When you let go of all images,  
all attempts to understand, describe, fix —  
**only pure Light remains,**  
in which form can be itself,  
and not what you named it.

This is the moment of Truth.  
When you do not look in order to see something —  
**but simply are present.**

And in this Presence  
distortions disappear,  
**and the real arises.**

</div>

***

<div class="lineated verse">

You cannot change the world  
without changing the gaze.

You cannot change another  
**without changing how you look at him.**

Therefore your gaze —  
is not simply an optical ray.  
**It is the fabric of perception,**  
on which you embroider the world.

</div>

***

<div class="lineated verse">

You think you are forming an opinion —  
**but in reality you creating a world.**

You believe you are simply perceiving —  
**but in reality you are shaping reality.**

It is the gaze  
that determines who you are,  
what you consider yourself,  
and what your path will be.

</div>

#### The image of the self is the main fruit of your gaze

<div class="lineated verse">

You look at yourself every day.  
But you do not see yourself —  
**you see your image.**

You look in the mirror —  
and you already know in advance  
what you "don't like",  
what is "aging",  
what is "worth improving".

But the body simply IS.  
The face simply IS.  
It is neither bad nor good —  
**before you looked at it.**

</div>

***

<div class="lineated verse">

You form your "I"  
not from what you are,  
**but from how you look at yourself.**

You consider yourself a failure,  
or a hero,  
or a victim,  
or a savior…

And each of these images  
**is born in the gaze.**

</div>

***

<div class="lineated verse">

Do you want to change your life?  
Change your gaze upon yourself.  
Do you want to heal relationships?  
Look differently.  
Do you want to find Light?  
**Look — with Light.**

Because you are not simply "one who sees".  
**You are the creator of the visible.**

And until you realize this,  
you will live in a world of reflections,  
taking them for the truth,  
suffering from that  
which you yourself have drawn.

**Everything you see,**  
**you yourself have built.**

</div>

### Chapter 25. Judgment in the Gaze. The Law of the Mirror

<div class="lineated verse">

You look —  
and you create another.

You think you are merely noticing —  
that he is lazy, selfish, stupid, proud…  
But in that moment you are not seeing him —  
**you are seeing your opinion.**

And this opinion is not just a sound in the head.  
**It is an internal verdict.**  
You passed it —  
**and it returned into you.**

</div>

***

<div class="lineated verse">

When you say:  
**"He is a bad person,"**  
you throw it outward, as it were.  
But reality works differently:  
everything you threw away —  
became your internal measure.

**You have become one who is capable of judging.**  
**And therefore — capable of judging yourself.**  
**And you will begin to do it.**

</div>

***

<div class="lineated verse">

*"With the measure you use, it will be measured to you."*

This is not a parable.  
**It is a mechanism.**

You see anger in others —  
and through this you become accustomed to anger as the norm.  
You see betrayal —  
and you install in yourself the expectation of betrayal.  
You look at the world with eyes of fear —  
and you begin to fear yourself.

</div>

***

<div class="lineated verse">

You judge —  
**and you yourself enter the cage**  
**that you have just built.**

Not because God judged you.  
**But because the gaze became your judge.**

</div>

***

<div class="lineated verse">

Do you not want to be judged?  
**Then do not judge.**

Not because it is a sin.  
**But because judgment is a form of thinking**  
that will inevitably turn back on you.

</div>

***

<div class="lineated verse">

Look at a mother  
who looks at her child with trust:  
he unfurls, he brightens,  
he wants to be what she sees in him.

Look at a woman  
whom a man looks at with adoration:  
she blossoms, even if she did not consider herself beautiful.

And conversely:  
if you look with disgust, with contempt,  
you do not simply record this —  
**you turn the other into your own reflection.**  
And then you hate him  
and through him — yourself.

</div>

***

<div class="lineated verse">

**Judgment is a gaze**  
**in which there is no room for God.**

**And that means — in which there is no room for you either.**  
There is only projection,  
fear,  
resentment,  
bitterness.  
But there is no Light.

</div>

***

<div class="lineated verse">

That is why judgment —  
is not an act of justice,  
**but an act of losing the Light.**

And every time you commit it,  
you move a little farther from yourself.  
And a little closer — to the shadow.

</div>

***

<div class="lineated verse">

But there is another path:  
**a gaze without judgment.**  
In it — there is no weakness.  
In it — is the power of Light,  
which does not need a verdict  
in order to be itself.

</div>

***

<div class="lineated verse">

You do not know the other —  
you know only the gaze with which you look at him.

If you want,  
I will continue this chapter  
and show how reality changes  
if you simply change your gaze.  
Do you want to?

You will say — people who judge right and left

often seem happy, successful and rich…

And you are right — that is how it is.  
You look at the world —  
and it seems:  
those who judge are not judged.  
They live in abundance,  
say what they think,  
criticize anyone —  
and nothing happens to them for it.

But look deeper.  
On the outside — success.  
**Inside — restlessness, fatigue,**  
**an inability to be in silence.**

They cannot stop,  
**because they are afraid of themselves.**

They run —  
not from others,  
but from their own gaze,  
which once judged.  
Now it is with them always.

</div>

#### Judging oneself

<div class="lineated verse">

Judgment of yourself —  
is not simply a bad thought.  
**It is a split.**

You, as it were, separate a part of yourself  
and put it on the docket.

</div>

<div class="lineated">

— Here you are insufficient.  
— Here you are weak.  
— You did this wrong.  
— You are unworthy of love.

</div>

<div class="lineated verse">

The words may be different.  
But the result is one:  
**an enemy appears inside you.**

Not an external one.  
**An internal one.**

</div>

***

<div class="lineated verse">

You are no longer whole.  
You are the one who looks,  
and the one who is looked upon.  
One condemns,  
the other — suffers.  
**And you are both.**

This is what judgment is.  
Not punishment, not lightning from the heavens.  
**But a constant leakage of energy**  
inside your own consciousness.

</div>

***

<div class="lineated verse">

You create within yourself  
a conflict —  
and call this **“development.”**

But there is no real growth there.  
There is only struggle.  
There is shame.  
There is fear of being exposed.

</div>

#### Where is karma here?

<div class="lineated verse">

Karma —  
is not about the next life.  
**Karma is the inertia of the gaze.**  
If you judge —  
you get used to looking that way.

It becomes your  
automatic background:  
**you see defects, mistakes, sins, guilt.**  
mistakes,  
sins,  
guilt.

And you can no longer see  
simply a Human.  
Simply yourself.  
Simply Light.

**This is a karmic knot:**  
a knot of perception.  
Not something mystical, but **your own habit** of **looking through judgment.**  
**but your own habit**  
**of looking through judgment.**

**An example.**

You are a father.  
A child broke a cup.  
You immediately think:  
— He is inattentive.  
— He doesn't listen.  
— He is doing it to spite me.

You scold him.  
The child is in tears.  
You walk away — and the thought returns:  
the thought returns:  
**“I am a bad father.”**

But you didn't untie the knot —  
**you simply changed the addressee of the judgment.**  
First — onto him,  
now — onto yourself.

This is how many live:  
between judgment of others  
and judgment of themselves.

But in this moment —  
you lose both.

You see neither the child,  
nor yourself.  
You see  
**a shadow,**  
**cast by your own gaze.**

</div>

#### How then to change this?

<div class="lineated verse">

Not through effort.  
Not through resistance.  
**But through attention.**

Catch this moment,  
when you want to condemn.

Freeze.  
And look,  
**at what exactly it is you are denying.**

And ask yourself the question:  
— And do I allow this of myself?

Often — no.  
This is why you cannot tolerate it in others.  
You become angry —  
not at them,  
**but at your shadow in them.**

</div>

***

<div class="lineated verse">

Everything that you judge in another —  
you have not accepted in yourself.

And until you see this —  
you will repeat it.  
And call it “karma.”  
**Though it is simply one and the same point of view, again and again.**  
again and again.

</div>

***

<div class="lineated verse">

Judgment is a loop.  
The Gaze is freedom.

When you learn to look  
without judgment,  
without the attempt to fix, to explain, to force…  
explain,  
force…  
**You let go of control,**  
and Light returns to you.

And then —  
both you and the other  
can be  
**themselves for the first time.**

</div>

***

<div class="lineated verse">

Want me to show you concrete steps —  
how to exit judgment and the knot of perception?  
**Not advice, but living actions, that can be applied right now.**  
that can be applied right now.

You want to get out.  
You feel it — this is a loop.  
You want to breathe.  
You are tired of being both the accused, the judge, and the jailer.  
and the judge,  
and the jailer.

And there is a way out.  
Simple.  
But not easy.

Because it demands  
not effort, but **stopping.**  
**but stopping.**

</div>

#### First step: Freeze

<div class="lineated verse">

When you catch yourself thinking:  
“He is a fool,”  
“She is fake,”  
“I am worthless,”  
“They are to blame” —  
**stop.**

Do not continue the thought.  
Do not argue with it.  
Do not try to replace it.

Simply  
**stop the movement of the gaze.**

It goes along a well-worn path.  
**But you can not follow.**

It is like stopping scratching a wound.  
You feel the itch,  
but you don't touch it.  
And it heals.

</div>

#### Second step: Look at the root

<div class="lineated verse">

**Ask: “What do I see?”**  
And answer — honestly.

Not “he acted badly.”  
But:  
— I see pain.  
— I see fear.  
— I see uncertainty.

**Often — my own.**

Look deeper.  
And say:  
“I see — a part of myself, that I do not want to see.”  
that I do not want to see.”

</div>

#### Third step: Embrace

<div class="lineated verse">

There is no need to love it immediately.  
That is false.

**But you can not push it away.**  
Not turn away.  
Not close yourself off.

You can say:  
**“Yes, you are here.**  
**I see you.**  
**And I will not abandon you.”**

This is a gaze  
**that does not judge,**  
**but holds.**

</div>

#### Fourth step: Give away

<div class="lineated verse">

Give this gaze to the Light.  
Say:  
“I do not wish to judge anymore.  
I wish to see You —  
in everything I see.”

And even if it doesn't work —  
**the intention has already freed you.**

Light begins to flow.  
The knot — melts.

</div>

#### Fifth step: Repeat

<div class="lineated verse">

This is not a one-time thing.  
You will see, how the habit of condemning will return.  
how the habit of condemning  
will return.

But now you are not in it.  
**Now you look at it.**

And in this lies the difference.

</div>

***

<div class="lineated verse">

You are no longer judgment.  
You are seeing.  
Without a label.  
Without accusation.  
Without division.

And when you look like this —  
everything you look at  
**returns to life.**

</div>

#### Small examples

<div class="lineated verse">

— You see a drunk on the street.  
Before — contempt.  
Now — a gaze: “Here is pain, hidden in a bottle.”  
**And in you — compassion.**  
This is you having exited judgment.

— You look in the mirror.  
Before — “aging,” “fat,” “not the one.”  
Now — “alive.”  
**And that is enough.**

— You hear someone shouting.  
Before — “aggressor,” “idiot.”  
Now — “unbearable pain with nowhere to go.”  
**You are no longer against.**  
**You are with them.**

And so the loop disappears.  
Thus presence is born.  
Thus Light returns.

</div>

***

<div class="lineated verse">

You want to understand, why you do not see the consequences of judgment right away.  
why you do not see the consequences of judgment right away.  
Why those who judge live as if unpunished.  
Why inside them there is a fire of destruction, and outside — the light of spotlights and success.  
and outside — the light of spotlights and success.

You want justice to be visible.  
But **Light does not work for show.**  
It works — **in the depth.**

</div>

***

<div class="lineated verse">

Judgment is not a “sin.”  
It is a **schema of perception.**  
Each time you judge,  
you create a **knot of perception**.  
It is like a fold in the fabric of consciousness.

You might not notice it.  
But now it is there.  
And you will look **through it.**

</div>

#### You judge — and lose your sight

<div class="lineated verse">

You said: “He is a deceitful person.”

And that's it — you no longer **see his true self.**  
Only this mask that you yourself hung on him.

First — onto him.  
Then — onto others.  
And then — onto yourself.

You no longer believe in anyone.  
You suspect everyone.  
You do not know how to see trust.

And you wonder:  
why can't you build closeness?  
why does no one open up to you?  
why are you always alone?

But **you yourself**  
**put darkness over your eyes.**

</div>

#### You judge yourself — and you seal off the living

<div class="lineated verse">

You said: “I am weak.” “I am a failure.” “I am ruined.”

And that's it — there is no space left in you,  
to be anything else.  
You confined yourself to a form,  
and then — **forgot that you made it up yourself.**

You no longer see a chance.  
You see no way out.  
You look — and see the confirmation of the verdict.  
And the longer you look —  
the more “real” it seems.

</div>

***

<div class="lineated verse">

Judging yourself is not honesty.  
It is a form of self-destruction.

</div>

#### You judge — and you receive a reflection

<div class="lineated verse">

You said about another:

“He will never achieve anything.”  
“He is a nobody.”  
“He is ridiculous.”

But that gaze **does not go into emptiness.**  
It — **reflects back.**

Not mystically.  
Not metaphysically.  
But **right here.**

You grow accustomed to seeing the world **without respect.**  
Without faith.  
Without light.

And soon you will begin to see yourself the same way.  
**Not as a body. But as not-valuable.**  
As someone who is not worthy of love, success, happiness.

And you will look for the reason —  
in others, in childhood, in fate.  
But it is — right here.  
**In one gaze.**  
Which you once cast —  
and it returned.

</div>

#### What is karma?

<div class="lineated verse">

It is not punishment.  
It is the **inertia of the gaze.**

You do not atone for sins.  
You simply  
**cannot see it differently,**  
**until you break the loop.**

And breaking it — is possible.  
How?

Through simple actions.

**Example.**

You were cruel to yourself.  
You constantly repeated: “I am nothing.”  
And everything inside tightened.

One day you are sitting by the window.  
And you suddenly notice:  
how beautiful the light is on the glass.

And inside you — warmth.  
And a thought:  
**“Maybe there is something good in me too?”**

You do not struggle.  
You **simply look differently.**  
And that — is already the beginning of liberation.

</div>

### Chapter 26. Judging Another — Cutting Yourself Off

<div class="lineated verse">

You say:  
“He is wrong”  
“He is stupid”  
“He is evil”  
“He does bad things”

But these are not just words.  
These are not just thoughts.  
**This is — the knife with which you cut the Body of the One.**

You do not notice —  
but each such gaze  
**is not only about him.**  
**It is about you.**

*You create two sides:*  
the one who is condemned —  
and the one who condemns.  
You seem to be saying:  
“I am not like that.”  
**But at that same moment you create duality,**  
**in which the Whole disappears.**

</div>

***

<div class="lineated verse">

You do not see the consequences immediately —  
but they come.  
**Not in the form of punishment,**  
**but in the form of isolation.**

**You separate yourself from the one you condemned,**  
**and therefore from yourself as well,**  
because that one is a part of you,  
a part of God,  
a part of the One.

And this is not philosophy.  
**This is — the concrete mechanics of consciousness.**

</div>

***

<div class="lineated verse">

When you say:  
“He is a traitor” —  
you separate in yourself that part,  
which once betrayed.  
You forbid yourself from being vulnerable, weak, alive.  
**You create a prison within yourself,**  
into which you imprison your own living self.

When you say:  
“He does not deserve love,”  
you are saying:  
“I too deserve it in some way not.”  
Because you have already applied the measure.  
You introduced the rule.  
And you yourself fall under it.

</div>

***

<div class="lineated verse">

**Judgment — is always a measure.**  
**And the measure always returns.**  
Not because someone judges you.  
**But because you yourself became the judge,**  
**and therefore — yourself entered the game of measure.**

**But God — is beyond measure.**  
He is in Love.

Do you want to remain with Him?  
**Then step out of judgment.**

</div>

***

<div class="lineated verse">

Do not judge — and you will remain Whole.  
Look — and see Yourself in another.  
Forgive — and you will become everything again.

**Judgment — is a mirror.**  
What you drew in it —  
that you became.  
Not outside.  
Inside.

</div>

#### How Judgment Works — From the Inside

<div class="lineated verse">

When you judge another,  
you seem to say:  
**“I am outside this.”**  
You build a wall —  
and you find yourself on one side,  
and life — on the other.

**But life — is not outside.**  
**It is — in you.**  
And every time you separate,  
you cut off a piece of yourself.

You said: “He is stupid.”  
And now, to confirm that thought,  
**your mind is forced to look for signs of an intelligent opposite in yourself —**  
otherwise who are you?  
**But this too is a loop.**  
Because now you are afraid of looking stupid.  
**You hide your vulnerability,**  
afraid to be imperfect.  
You lock yourself in a cell —  
the very one you threw the other into.

</div>

***

<div class="lineated verse">

You said: “He is ugly.”  
**Now you will measure yourself by beauty.**  
Compare.  
Fear growing old.  
Fear being rejected.  
Fear being seen.  
You yourself became a slave to that measure,  
which you let loose into the world.

</div>

***

<div class="lineated verse">

You said: “He is a bad father.”  
**Now you are afraid of making mistakes with your children.**  
**You will judge yourself for the slightest mistakes.**  
You will suffer —  
not because you are bad,  
**but because you let judgment into yourself.**

</div>

***

<div class="lineated verse">

Judgment — is not just a gaze.  
**It is — a cell,**  
**which closes access to the Light**  
in that part of your heart,  
where you placed a sign:  
“This is inadmissible.”

</div>

***

<div class="lineated verse">

**But the Light — always looks with love.**  
It does not label.  
It does not brand.  
It sees —  
**and accepts.**

Because in God there is no “he and I.”  
There is only “I.”

</div>

***

<div class="lineated verse">

Every time you condemned another,  
**you sentenced yourself to a life in a divided world.**  
This is judgment.  
**It is — within the gaze,**  
not in the future.

And it does not punish.  
**It separates.**

</div>

***

<div class="lineated verse">

Jesus said:  
“With the judgment you judge, you shall be judged.”  
This is not a threat.  
This is — a description of the law.

You look —  
and you become that,  
which you made of the other  
in your gaze.

</div>

#### Why does it seem "not by the same measure"?

<div class="lineated verse">

You say:  
“I judged —  
but I did not feel the reciprocal measure.  
I called someone names,  
and I remained unharmed.  
Where is the promised payment?”  
But the payment does not come from outside.  
**It is already inside.**

</div>

***

<div class="lineated verse">

Judgment — is not always pain.  
**Sometimes — insensitivity.**  
You judge,  
**and within you subtlety dies out.**  
You no longer hear,  
no longer feel.  
**You coarsen.**

You judge, and your heart constricts —  
but you call this  
“character,”  
“reasonableness,”  
“clarity of judgment.”

</div>

***

<div class="lineated verse">

**You judge, and you lose the taste for life.**  
It goes away imperceptibly.  
You simply no longer rejoice for no reason.  
You begin to demand.  
To compare.  
To expect.

**You judge, and you become lonely.**  
Not because you were abandoned.  
**But because you cut yourself off from others.**

</div>

***

<div class="lineated verse">

You see:  
a judging person can be successful,  
strong, influential.

**But what does he feel at night, in solitude?**  
What does he hide, even from himself?  
What walls has he built inside?

</div>

***

<div class="lineated verse">

Judgment rarely comes as punishment.  
**It comes as a change of the field itself.**  
You no longer see the Light,  
because your gaze has become clouded.

And you do not understand,  
**that this is the answer.**

</div>

***

<div class="lineated verse">

**The measure is the same,**  
but you do not recognize it,  
**because you yourself have changed.**

You did not pay with pain —  
**you paid with the loss of Light.**  
And it goes away —  
without noise.

</div>

***

<div class="lineated verse">

This is not punishment.  
This is a consequence.

Judgment — is not God's design.  
**It is the law of reflection.**  
You look —  
**and you become what you see.**

</div>

***

<div class="lineated verse">

Do you want me to show this  
with specific examples from life?  
So that you can recognize judgment —  
in yourself.

</div>

#### Judgment in Everyday Life: The Invisible Measure, But an Accurate Reflection

<div class="lineated verse">

**Example 1: “He is stupid.”**

You look at another,  
and inside you form:  
**“He is stupid.”**

Outwardly — nothing.  
You continue communicating,  
maybe even politely.

But inside  
your measure has already been passed:  
**he is lower**.  
**you are higher**.

What happens?

You lose the ability  
to **learn** from him.  
After all, what could a stupid person teach you?

You don't notice the simple truths  
that he might have brought.  
You become **closed**.  
Not towards him —  
**towards Life.**

That is the judgment by the same measure:  
**you stop growing.**  
You condemned stupidity —  
and became incapable of receiving wisdom.

Not because it is not there,  
but because **you cut it off.**

**Example 2: “She is frivolous.”**

You look at a woman,  
see lightness, spontaneity, playfulness —  
and you judge:  
**“Superficial.”**

In that moment  
you cut off within yourself  
**access to joy.**

You become “deep,”  
“intelligent,” “serious.”

But when the desire awakens in you  
to be **alive** —  
to laugh, to rejoice —  
**you cannot.**

You condemned that as “superficial”.  
You closed the path to yourself.  
**By the same measure.**

**Example 3: “He is arrogant.”**

You sense:  
the person is closed,  
keeps distance,  
is not friendly.

You judge:  
**“He is full of himself.”**

In that moment  
you yourself become **such.**  
You are no longer open.  
You closed yourself off from him —  
and became **his reflection.**

Now two people  
look at each other —  
through a wall.

Who started?  
Who was first?  
**It does not matter.**

The main thing —  
**now you are in that wall too.**

</div>

***

<div class="lineated verse">

You just wanted  
to give an evaluation.  
But you **formed yourself.**  
Into every gaze —  
you **become.**

</div>

#### This is what judgment is: not a verdict, but a transformation

<div class="lineated verse">

You look —  
and you transform  
into the one who looks **not with eyes, but with judgment.**

And you no longer see the Light —  
not even in yourself.

If you want,  
I will show you how to get out of this.  
How to purify the gaze —  
and return to yourself.

</div>

#### How to exit judgment: The Purification of the Gaze and the Return to the Self

<div class="lineated verse">

You must not judge yourself  
for having judged others.  
That is a new turn of the trap.  
You can simply **see**  
how the gaze works —  
and return it **to the Light.**

</div>

#### 1. Recognition

<div class="lineated verse">

The first thing is to see:  
**I judged.**  
Not to deny, not to justify.  
Simply to say honestly:  
**“Yes, I looked that way.”**

You are not guilty.  
You simply forgot,  
that the gaze is an **act of creation**.

</div>

#### 2. Returning the Gaze

<div class="lineated verse">

Now — gently,  
without violence —  
turn the gaze back.  
Not towards the person.  
But **into yourself.**

Ask:  
**What in me is afraid of being what I condemned?**  
Why did I not allow this form to be?

You will see:  
behind every judgment  
— **fear.**  
Fear of being stupid.  
Abandoned.  
Unimportant.  
Unloved.  
And you create an image  
in which you are better,  
in order to hide the pain.

</div>

#### 3. Opening Space

<div class="lineated verse">

Now — simply look  
at the one you judged —  
**without a story.**

Do not call him anything.  
Do not define him.  
Simply look  
in Silence.

You will see:  
**he is alive.**  
**He is like you.**  
**He is also Light.**

</div>

#### 4. And this is what happens

<div class="lineated verse">

You no longer judge.  
And you yourself are no longer afraid  
to be what you condemned.

You return to yourself  
**that part from which you fled.**

And now you — are **whole.**  
Not perfect.  
Not right.  
Not ideal.

But **whole**.  
**Present.**  
**Gazing from the Light.**

</div>

#### Practice: How to Exit Judgment

<div class="lineated verse">

Close your eyes.  
Take a breath —  
and do not exhale until you hear,  
that you are here.  
The breath is not for air,  
but for **presence.**

Now — allow the image to surface  
of the one you recently judged.  
Do not look for someone “important.”  
Let it be anyone  
you looked at with irritation,  
disdain, arrogance,  
even if you did not express it in words.

Look at them within yourself.  
As if they stand before you.  
Do not flee.  
Do not explain.  
**Simply be.**

</div>

Now say (within):

<div class="lineated verse">

**“I see that I judged you.**  
**I gave you a label.**  
**I separated you from myself.**  
**And by doing so, I separated myself — from the Light.”**

Now — take another breath.  
And look **without a label.**  
Release the thoughts.
